## **Phase 2: Minimum Playable Path (3-5 days)**

**Create a single, complete gameplay loop:**

### **Day 1: Player Creation & Tutorial**
```
1. Start new game
2. Create character (name, starting stats)
3. Tutorial combat (teaches basic mechanics)
4. First quest given
```

### **Day 2: World Navigation**
```
1. Map scene with 3-5 locations
2. Click to travel between areas
3. Encounter system (combat, events, NPCs)
4. Return to town hub
```

### **Day 3: Combat Integration**
```
1. Random encounter triggers CombatScene
2. Combat uses your existing systems
3. Victory → rewards (gold, XP, loot)
4. Return to MapScene
```

### **Day 4: Progression Loop**
```
1. Level up from combat
2. Visit shop to spend gold
3. Equip new items
4. Unlock new skills
5. Return to exploring
```

### **Day 5: Quest Completion**
```
1. Complete first quest objective
2. Return to quest giver
3. Receive quest rewards
4. Get next quest
Phase 3: System Integration Checklist

    <!-- Phaser will inject the game canvas here -->
    
    <!-- Load Phaser 3 from CDN -->
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/phaser@3.60.0/dist/phaser.min.js"></script>
    
    <!-- Load your game code -->
    <script type="module" src="src/main.js"></script>
</body>
</html>
STEP 3: CREATE main.js (GAME STARTUP)
This is where Phaser starts:

javascript
// src/main.js

import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
import MenuScene from './scenes/MenuScene.js';
import GameScene from './scenes/GameScene.js';
import CombatScene from './scenes/CombatScene.js';

// Phaser game configuration
const config = {
    type: Phaser.AUTO,
    width: 1280,
    height: 720,
    backgroundColor: '#1a1a1a',
    parent: 'game-container',
    
    physics: {
        default: 'arcade',
        arcade: {
            debug: false,
            gravity: { y: 0 }
        }
    },
    
    scene: [
        BootScene,    // First: Load assets
        MenuScene,    // Second: Show menu
        GameScene,    // Third: Main game
        CombatScene   // Fourth: Combat
    ],
    
    scale: {
        mode: Phaser.Scale.FIT,
        autoCenter: Phaser.Scale.CENTER_BOTH
    }
};

// START THE GAME
const game = new Phaser.Game(config);

// Expose game globally for debugging
window.game = game;
STEP 4: CREATE BootScene.js (LOADS EVERYTHING)
javascript
// src/scenes/BootScene.js

export default class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'BootScene' });
    }
    
    preload() {
        // Create loading bar
        this.createLoadingBar();
        
        // Load placeholder graphics (you can replace with real assets later)
        this.loadPlaceholders();
        
        // Load your data files
        this.load.json('enemies', 'assets/data/enemies.json');
        this.load.json('skills', 'assets/data/skills.json');
        this.load.json('equipment', 'assets/data/equipment.json');
    }
    
    create() {
        console.log('✅ Assets loaded!');
        
        // Go to menu
        this.scene.start('MenuScene');
    }
    
    createLoadingBar() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        const progressBar = this.add.graphics();
        const progressBox = this.add.graphics();
        progressBox.fillStyle(0x222222, 0.8);
        progressBox.fillRect(width / 2 - 160, height / 2 - 25, 320, 50);
        
        const loadingText = this.add.text(width / 2, height / 2 - 50, 'Loading...', {
            font: '20px monospace',
            fill: '#ffffff'
        });
        loadingText.setOrigin(0.5, 0.5);
        
        const percentText = this.add.text(width / 2, height / 2, '0%', {
            font: '18px monospace',
            fill: '#ffffff'
        });
        percentText.setOrigin(0.5, 0.5);
        
        this.load.on('progress', (value) => {
            percentText.setText(parseInt(value * 100) + '%');
            progressBar.clear();
            progressBar.fillStyle(0x44ff44, 1);
            progressBar.fillRect(width / 2 - 150, height / 2 - 15, 300 * value, 30);
        });
        
        this.load.on('complete', () => {
            progressBar.destroy();
            progressBox.destroy();
            loadingText.destroy();
            percentText.destroy();
        });
    }
    
    loadPlaceholders() {
        // Create colored rectangles as placeholders
        const graphics = this.make.graphics({ x: 0, y: 0, add: false });
        
        // Player placeholder
        graphics.fillStyle(0x44ff44, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('player', 64, 64);
        graphics.clear();
        
        // Enemy placeholder
        graphics.fillStyle(0xff4444, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('enemy', 64, 64);
        graphics.clear();
        
        // UI button
        graphics.fillStyle(0x4444ff, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 200, 50);
        graphics.generateTexture('button', 200, 50);
    }
}
STEP 5: CREATE MenuScene.js (TITLE SCREEN)
javascript
// src/scenes/MenuScene.js

export default class MenuScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'MenuScene' });
    }
    
    create() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Title
        this.add.text(width / 2, height / 3, 'VERDANCE', {
            fontSize: '72px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#44ff44',
            fontStyle: 'bold'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Subtitle
        this.add.text(width / 2, height / 3 + 80, 'Tactical RPG', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#88ff88'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // New Game button
        const newGameBtn = this.add.text(width / 2, height / 2 + 50, '► NEW GAME', {
            fontSize: '32px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#333333',
            padding: { x: 20, y: 10 }
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        newGameBtn.setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        newGameBtn.on('pointerover', () => {
            newGameBtn.setStyle({ backgroundColor: '#44ff44', color: '#000000' });
        });
        
        newGameBtn.on('pointerout', () => {
            newGameBtn.setStyle({ backgroundColor: '#333333', color: '#ffffff' });
        });
        
        newGameBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            console.log('🎮 Starting new game...');
            this.scene.start('GameScene');
        });
        
        // Instructions
        this.add.text(width / 2, height - 50, 'Click "NEW GAME" to start', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#888888'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
    }
}
STEP 6: CREATE GameScene.js (MAIN GAME)
javascript
// src/scenes/GameScene.js

import PlayerManager from '../systems/PlayerManager.js';
import CombatManager from '../systems/CombatManager.js';

export default class GameScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'GameScene' });
    }
    
    create() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Initialize systems
        this.playerManager = new PlayerManager(this);
        
        // Create player
        this.player = this.add.sprite(width / 2, height / 2, 'player');
        
        // UI
        this.add.text(20, 20, 'VERDANCE - Main Game', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            color: '#44ff44'
        });
        
        // Player stats
        this.statsText = this.add.text(20, 60, '', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#ffffff'
        });
        this.updateStatsDisplay();
        
        // Combat button
        const combatBtn = this.add.text(width / 2, height - 100, '⚔ START COMBAT', {
            fontSize: '28px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#ff4444',
            padding: { x: 20, y: 10 }
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        combatBtn.setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        combatBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            console.log('⚔ Entering combat...');
            this.scene.start('CombatScene', {
                playerData: this.playerManager.getState()
            });
        });
        
        // Instructions
        this.add.text(width / 2, height - 50, 'Click "START COMBAT" to fight', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#888888'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
    }
    
    updateStatsDisplay() {
        const stats = this.playerManager.getState();
        this.statsText.setText([
            `Level: ${stats.level}`,
            `HP: ${stats.currentHp}/${stats.maxHp}`,
            `DSP: ${stats.currentDsp}/${stats.maxDsp}`,
            `Attack: ${stats.attack}`,
            `Defense: ${stats.defense}`
        ]);
    }
}
STEP 7: CREATE CombatScene.js (COMBAT)
javascript
// src/scenes/CombatScene.js

import CombatManager from '../systems/CombatManager.js';
import EnemyManager from '../systems/EnemyManager.js';

export default class CombatScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'CombatScene' });
    }
    
    init(data) {
        this.playerData = data.playerData;
    }
    
    create() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Initialize combat
        this.combatManager = new CombatManager(this);
        this.enemyManager = new EnemyManager(this);
        
        // Title
        this.add.text(width / 2, 30, '⚔ COMBAT ⚔', {
            fontSize: '32px',
            color: '#ff4444'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Player sprite
        this.playerSprite = this.add.sprite(200, height / 2, 'player');
        this.add.text(200, height / 2 + 60, 'PLAYER', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#44ff44'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Enemy sprite
        this.enemySprite = this.add.sprite(width - 200, height / 2, 'enemy');
        this.add.text(width - 200, height / 2 + 60, 'ENEMY', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#ff4444'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Combat UI
        this.createCombatUI();
        
        // Start combat
        this.startCombat();
    }
    
    createCombatUI() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Attack button
        const attackBtn = this.add.text(width / 2 - 120, height - 100, '⚔ ATTACK', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#ff4444',
            padding: { x: 15, y: 8 }
        }).setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        attackBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            this.playerAttack();
        });
        
        // Skill button
        const skillBtn = this.add.text(width / 2 + 20, height - 100, '✨ SKILL', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#4444ff',
            padding: { x: 15, y: 8 }
        }).setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        skillBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            this.playerSkill();
        });
        
        // Combat log
        this.combatLog = this.add.text(20, height - 180, '', {
            fontSize: '14px',
            color: '#ffffff'
        });
    }
    
    startCombat() {
        this.logMessage('Combat started!');
        this.playerHp = 100;
        this.enemyHp = 80;
        this.updateDisplay();
    }
    
    playerAttack() {
        const damage = Math.floor(Math.random() * 20) + 10;
        this.enemyHp -= damage;
        this.logMessage(`You dealt ${damage} damage!`);
        
        // Flash enemy
        this.tweens.add({
            targets: this.enemySprite,
            tint: 0xff0000,
            duration: 100,
            yoyo: true
        });
        
        this.updateDisplay();
        this.checkCombatEnd();
        
        if (this.enemyHp > 0) {
            this.time.delayedCall(1000, () => this.enemyAttack());
        }
    }
    
    playerSkill() {
        const damage = Math.floor(Math.random() * 30) + 20;
        this.enemyHp -= damage;
        this.logMessage(`You used a skill for ${damage} damage!`);
        
        // Flash enemy
        this.tweens.add({
            targets: this.enemySprite,
            tint: 0x4444ff,
            duration: 150,
            yoyo: true,
            repeat: 1
        });
        
        this.updateDisplay();
        this.checkCombatEnd();
        
        if (this.enemyHp > 0) {
            this.time.delayedCall(1000, () => this.enemyAttack());
        }
    }
    
    enemyAttack() {
        const damage = Math.floor(Math.random() * 15) + 5;
        this.playerHp -= damage;
        this.logMessage(`Enemy dealt ${damage} damage!`);
        
        // Flash player
        this.tweens.add({
            targets: this.playerSprite,
            tint: 0xff0000,
            duration: 100,
            yoyo: true
        });
        
        this.updateDisplay();
        this.checkCombatEnd();
    }
    
    checkCombatEnd() {
        if (this.enemyHp <= 0) {
            this.logMessage('💚 VICTORY! 💚');
            this.time.delayedCall(2000, () => {
                this.scene.start('GameScene');
            });
        } else if (this.playerHp <= 0) {
            this.logMessage('💀 DEFEAT 💀');
            this.time.delayedCall(2000, () => {
                this.scene.start('MenuScene');
            });
        }
    }
    
    updateDisplay() {
        // Update HP bars (simplified text for now)
        this.add.text(200, height / 2 - 80, `HP: ${Math.max(0, this.playerHp)}`, {
            fontSize: '18px',
            color: '#44ff44'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        this.add.text(width - 200, height / 2 - 80, `HP: ${Math.max(0, this.enemyHp)}`, {
            fontSize: '18px',
            color: '#ff4444'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
    }
    
    logMessage(text) {
        console.log(text);
        this.combatLog.setText(text);
    }
}

Architected comprehensive beginner guide covering Phaser fundamentals and Cursor utility
Architected comprehensive beginner guide covering Phaser fundamentals and Cursor utility
🎓 COMPLETE BEGINNER'S GUIDE: BUILDING YOUR GAME
Let me explain everything from the ground up, assuming you're new to this.

🧠 PART 1: UNDERSTANDING THE FUNDAMENTALS
What is Phaser?
Phaser is a game framework that does the hard work for you:

Draws graphics on screen
Handles mouse clicks and keyboard input
Manages game loops (updating 60 times per second)
Loads images and sounds
Handles physics and collisions
Think of Phaser as a movie projector + stage + actors all in one.

What are "Scenes"?
A Scene is like a page in a book or a room in a house:

MenuScene = The title screen room
GameScene = The main gameplay room
CombatScene = The battle arena room
You move between scenes just like clicking through pages or walking through doors.

javascript
// Going from Menu to Game:
this.scene.start('GameScene'); // "Walk through door to GameScene"
How Does a Game Loop Work?
Every game runs in a loop 60 times per second:

javascript
// Phaser does this automatically:
while (gameIsRunning) {
    1. Check for input (did player click?)
    2. Update game state (move characters, check HP)
    3. Draw everything on screen
    4. Wait 1/60th of a second
    5. Repeat
}
You don't write this loop - Phaser does it for you. You just write:

create() - Runs once when scene starts
update() - Runs 60 times per second
What are Modules/Imports?
Modern JavaScript splits code into files:

javascript
// In CombatManager.js - you EXPORT the class
export default class CombatManager {
    // ... code ...
}

// In CombatScene.js - you IMPORT it
import CombatManager from '../systems/CombatManager.js';
```

**Think of it like shipping packages:**
- **Export** = "Put this in a box and ship it out"
- **Import** = "Receive the package and open it"

STEP 3: Create index.html

Click "New File"

Paste this code:
html
<!DOCTYPE html>

        }
    </style>
</head>
<body>
    <!-- Phaser library -->
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/phaser@3.60.0/dist/phaser.min.js"></script>
    
    <!-- Your game -->
    <script type="module" src="src/main.js"></script>
</body>
</html>
What this does:

Line 1-4: Basic HTML structure
Line 5-13: Makes page black and centers game
Line 17: Loads Phaser from internet (no install needed!)
Line 20: Loads YOUR game code
STEP 4: Create main.js (Game Startup)
Create file: src/main.js
Paste this:
javascript
// src/main.js

// This will import your scenes (we'll create them next)
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
import MenuScene from './scenes/MenuScene.js';

// Configure Phaser
const config = {
    type: Phaser.AUTO,           // Use best graphics mode
    width: 1280,                 // Game window width
    height: 720,                 // Game window height
    backgroundColor: '#1a1a1a',  // Dark background
    
    // Which scenes to use
    scene: [
        BootScene,   // First scene (loading)
        MenuScene    // Second scene (menu)
    ]
};

// START THE GAME
const game = new Phaser.Game(config);
console.log('🎮 Game started!');
What this does:

Lines 4-5: Get your scene files (we'll create these next)
Lines 8-19: Tell Phaser how big the game is and which scenes to use
Line 22: Actually starts the game
STEP 5: Create BootScene.js (Loading Screen)
Create file: src/scenes/BootScene.js
Paste this:
javascript
// src/scenes/BootScene.js

export default class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'BootScene' });
    }
    
    preload() {
        // This runs FIRST - load assets here
        console.log('📦 Loading assets...');
        
        // Show loading text
        this.add.text(640, 360, 'LOADING...', {
            fontSize: '48px',
            color: '#ffffff'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Create placeholder graphics
        this.createPlaceholders();
    }
    
    create() {
        // This runs AFTER preload
        console.log('✅ Assets loaded!');
        
        // Go to menu after 1 second
        this.time.delayedCall(1000, () => {
            this.scene.start('MenuScene');
        });
    }
    
    createPlaceholders() {
        // Create simple colored squares as temporary graphics
        const graphics = this.make.graphics({ x: 0, y: 0, add: false });
        
        // Green square for player
        graphics.fillStyle(0x44ff44, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('player', 64, 64);
        graphics.clear();
        
        // Red square for enemy
        graphics.fillStyle(0xff4444, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('enemy', 64, 64);
    }
}
What each function does:

constructor() - Runs when scene is created. Names the scene 'BootScene'
preload() - Loads images, sounds, data. Runs BEFORE anything shows
create() - Sets up the scene. Runs AFTER preload
createPlaceholders() - Makes simple colored squares to use instead of images
Key Phaser methods:

this.add.text() - Puts text on screen
this.time.delayedCall() - Wait, then do something
this.scene.start() - Switch to different scene
STEP 6: Create MenuScene.js (Title Screen)
Create file: src/scenes/MenuScene.js
Paste this:
javascript
// src/scenes/MenuScene.js

export default class MenuScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'MenuScene' });
    }
    
    create() {
        console.log('📺 Showing menu...');
        
        // Game title
        this.add.text(640, 200, 'VERDANCE', {
            fontSize: '72px',
            color: '#44ff44',
            fontStyle: 'bold'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Start button
        const startButton = this.add.text(640, 400, '▶ START GAME', {
            fontSize: '32px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#333333',
            padding: { x: 20, y: 10 }
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Make button clickable
        startButton.setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        // When mouse hovers over button
        startButton.on('pointerover', () => {
            startButton.setStyle({ 
                backgroundColor: '#44ff44',
                color: '#000000'
            });
        });
        
        // When mouse leaves button
        startButton.on('pointerout', () => {
            startButton.setStyle({ 
                backgroundColor: '#333333',
                color: '#ffffff'
            });
        });
        
        // When button is clicked
        startButton.on('pointerdown', () => {
            console.log('🎮 Starting game!');
            // TODO: Start game scene (we'll add this later)
            alert('Game would start here!');
        });
    }
}
```

**What this does:**
- Line 12-16: Creates big green title
- Line 19-24: Creates button with text
- Line 27: Makes button clickable (cursor becomes pointer)
- Line 30-35: Button changes color on hover
- Line 38-42: Button returns to normal when mouse leaves
- Line 45-49: What happens when clicked

---

### **STEP 7: Run Your Game**

**Option A: Using Live Server in Cursor**

1. In Cursor, install "Live Server" extension:
   - Click Extensions icon (left sidebar)
   - Search "Live Server"
   - Click Install

2. Right-click `index.html`
3. Click "Open with Live Server"
4. Browser opens automatically!

**Option B: Using Terminal**

1. Open Terminal in Cursor (View → Terminal)
2. Type: `npx http-server -p 8000`
3. Open browser to: `http://localhost:8000`

**What you should see:**
1. "LOADING..." text for 1 second
2. Menu with green "VERDANCE" title
3. Clickable "START GAME" button
4. Alert when you click button

🆘 COMMON BEGINNER MISTAKES
1. Forgetting export default
javascript
// ❌ WRONG
class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    
}

// ✅ CORRECT
export default class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    
}
2. Wrong file paths in imports
javascript
// ❌ WRONG - missing ../
import BootScene from 'scenes/BootScene.js';

// ✅ CORRECT - goes up one folder (..) then into scenes
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
3. Forgetting .js extension
javascript
// ❌ WRONG
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene';

// ✅ CORRECT
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
```

### **4. Opening index.html directly**
```
❌ WRONG: Double-click index.html
(Shows errors about modules)

✅ CORRECT: Use Live Server or http-server
(Serves files properly)
```

Mar 7

Architected tactical positioning mechanics integrating flanking, covered attacks, and thematic Verdance systems
Architected tactical positioning mechanics integrating flanking, covered attacks, and thematic Verdance systems
🎯 VERDANCE POSITIONING MECHANICS - COMPLETE REDESIGN
Let me analyze your systems and redesign these positioning mechanics to fit perfectly with your Verdance tactical hex-grid combat.

📊 CURRENT ISSUES TO FIX
Problems with generic positioning:

"Flanking" is vague (rear? side? how many allies?)
"High ground" doesn't fit hex grids well
"Cover" needs Verdance theming (roots, vines, not walls)
No integration with ZoC, Essence, or Pure/Blighted mechanics
Your game needs Verdance-specific positioning that:

Uses hex adjacency clearly
Integrates with ZoC triggers
Rewards faction synergies (Pure chains, Blight spreads)
Feels organic (roots, canopy, terrain)
🌿 NEW VERDANCE POSITIONING SYSTEM
1. ENTANGLEMENT (Replaces "Flanking")
Concept: Verdance combat is about surrounding and ensnaring enemies in living terrain (roots, vines, spores). Multiple allies create an "Entanglement Net."

How It Works:

ENTANGLED STATUS achieved when:

Ally Encirclement: Enemy has 2+ allied units adjacent to them (any hex face)
OR Skill Trigger: Abilities like "Vine Lash" or "Spore Web" apply Entangled status
OR ZoC Overlap: Enemy is in 2+ overlapping Zones of Control
Visual Indicator: Green vine chains appear between allies surrounding the target

ENTANGLEMENT BONUSES:

Base Entangled (2 allies): +15% damage, enemy -1 Movement
Deep Entangled (3+ allies): +25% damage, enemy -2 Movement, +10% crit
Rooted Entangled (4+ allies): +35% damage, enemy immobilized
Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Entanglement creates healing aura (+5 Vital Thrum/turn to allies)
Blighted: Entanglement spreads Blight DoT (+2 stacks per turn to target)
Example:

Hex Grid Visual:

    [Vine Knight]
   /            \
[Enemy]        [Spore Caller]
   \            /
    [Tree Sentinel]

= Deep Entangled (3 allies adjacent)
= Enemy: +25% damage taken, -2 Movement, +10% crit against them
= Pure bonus: All 3 allies gain +5 Vital Thrum/turn
2. SHROUDED STRIKE (Replaces "Rear Attack" → "Covered Attack")
Concept: Verdance fighters use natural cover (canopy, roots, mist) to launch devastating ambushes from concealment.

How It Works:

SHROUDED STATUS achieved when:

Terrain Cover: Attacker is in Forest, Spore Cloud, Shadow Veil, or Overgrowth hex
AND Position: Target cannot see attacker (blocked line of sight by terrain/allies)
OR Ability: Skills like "Veil Step" or "Mist Cloak" grant Shrouded for 1 turn
SHROUDED STRIKE BONUSES:

Partial Shroud (1 cover element): +20% damage, ignore 25% defense
Full Shroud (2+ elements): +40% damage, ignore 50% defense, guaranteed crit
Assassin Shroud (Veilwalker class in Full Shroud): +60% damage, apply Fear
Breaks on: First attack from Shroud (becomes visible), or if enemy has "True Sight"

Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Shrouded Strike also heals attacker for 15% damage dealt
Blighted: Shrouded Strike applies "Infected Wound" (3-turn DoT)
Example:

Hex Grid Visual:

[Forest] [Forest] [Enemy] [Open]
   ↑        ↑
[Moonshade Ranger in Forest] attacks [Enemy]

Enemy can't see through dense forest
= Full Shroud achieved
= +40% damage, ignore 50% defense, guaranteed crit
3. CANOPY ADVANTAGE (Replaces "High Ground")
Concept: In Verdance's vertical forests, fighting from treetops/vines gives tactical superiority.

How It Works:

CANOPY TIERS:

Ground Level (0): Default, no bonuses
Root Level (-1): Underground, +20% defense, -10% accuracy
Canopy (+1): Tree level, bonuses below
Sky Canopy (+2): Highest branches, maximum bonuses
CANOPY ADVANTAGE BONUSES (when attacking lower tier):

+1 Tier Advantage (Canopy → Ground): 
  - Ranged: +20% accuracy, +10% Spore Drift damage
  - Melee: +15% damage (leaping strikes)
  
+2 Tier Advantage (Sky → Ground):
  - Ranged: +35% accuracy, +20% Spore Drift damage
  - Melee: +25% damage + knockback
Movement Between Tiers:

Costs Movement: 2 hexes to climb/descend 1 tier
Abilities override: "Vine Swing" ignores cost, "Sky Leap" moves 2 tiers instantly
Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Canopy Advantage grants +1 Essence per turn (sunlight absorption)
Blighted: Ground/Root Advantage grants +1 Essence per turn (rot feeding)
Example:

Vertical Grid:

[Sky Canopy (+2)]    [Veilwalker]
[Canopy (+1)]        [Empty]
[Ground (0)]         [Enemy]

Veilwalker attacks from Sky (+2) to Ground (0)
= +2 tier advantage
= Ranged: +35% accuracy, +20% Spore Drift damage
4. VERDANT WARD (Replaces "Cover")
Concept: Living terrain (roots, brambles, fungal growth) provides organic protection that can be manipulated.

How It Works:

WARD TERRAIN TYPES:

Light Ward (Grass, Moss): -15% damage taken
Medium Ward (Brambles, Roots): -30% damage taken, attackers take 5 damage
Heavy Ward (Ancient Trees, Fungal Walls): -50% damage taken, reflect 20% damage
Interactive Ward:

Pure Units: Can spend 2 Lumen Essence to strengthen ward (+10% protection for 2 turns)
Blighted Units: Can spend 2 Blight Essence to corrupt ward (becomes hazard, deals 5 DoT/turn to enemies)
Destructible: Heavy attacks (20+ damage) destroy ward terrain
Positional Ward Stacking:

Ward + Ally Adjacent: Additional -10% damage
Ward + ZoC Active: Additional -15% damage  
Ward + Entangled Enemy: Ward becomes "Living Prison" (enemy -50% all stats)
Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Ward heals (+5 Vital Thrum/turn)
Blighted: Ward spreads Blight to adjacent hexes (terrain corruption)
Example:

[Heavy Ward Hex] ← [Vine Knight]
        ↓
    [Enemy attacking]

Vine Knight in Ancient Tree Ward
= -50% damage taken
= Enemy takes 20% reflected damage
= Vine Knight has ally adjacent: -60% total damage taken
⚔️ COMPLETE POSITIONING MECHANICS TABLE

Architected thematic positioning system integrating faction mechanics and terrain
Architected thematic positioning system integrating faction mechanics and terrain
🌿 VERDANCE POSITIONING MECHANICS - COMPLETE SYSTEM REDESIGN
Looking at your comprehensive Verdance systems, I need to redesign positioning to integrate perfectly with your hex-grid ZoC, Essence system, Pure/Blighted factions, and Verdance terrain. Let me create a positioning framework that feels organic and tactical.

🎯 THE FOUR PILLARS OF VERDANCE POSITIONING
1. ENTANGLEMENT (Replaces "Flanking")
Concept: In Verdance, combat is about ensnaring enemies in living matter - vines, roots, spores, soul-bonds. Multiple allies create an "Entanglement Net."

How to Achieve:

ENTANGLED STATUS when:
├─ 2+ Allied units adjacent to enemy (any hex face)
├─ OR Skill-triggered (Vine Lash, Spore Web, Soul Bind)
└─ OR ZoC Overlap (enemy in 2+ overlapping Zones of Control)
Hex Grid Visual:

    [Vine Knight]
   /            \
[Enemy]        [Spore Caller]
   \            /
    [Your Unit attacking]

= 3 units adjacent to enemy = Deep Entanglement
ENTANGLEMENT BONUSES:

Tier	Requirement	Offensive Bonus	Control Effect	Visual
Base Entangled	2 allies adjacent	+15% Thorn Lash/Spore Drift	Enemy -1 Rhizome Stride	Green vine chains appear
Deep Entangled	3+ allies adjacent	+25% damage, +10% crit	Enemy -2 Stride, can't teleport	Pulsing root cage
Rooted	4+ allies OR skill	+35% damage, ignore Bark Ward	Immobilized completely	Massive root prison
Faction-Specific Entanglement:

Pure (Lumen):

Entanglement creates Bloom Aura → +5 Vital Thrum/turn to all entangling allies
Even Essence rolls while maintaining Entanglement → chain heal spreads to adjacent Pure units
Blighted:

Entanglement applies Rot Spread → +2 Blight DoT stacks per turn to target
Odd Essence rolls while maintaining Entanglement → DoT spreads to all enemies within 2 hexes
2. SHROUDED STRIKE (Replaces "Rear Attack" → "Covered Attack")
Concept: Verdance fighters use natural concealment (forest canopy, spore clouds, shadow veils, fungal mists) to launch devastating ambushes.

How to Achieve:

SHROUDED STATUS when:
├─ Attacker in concealing terrain (Forest, Spore Cloud, Shadow Veil, Overgrowth)
├─ AND Target cannot see attacker (blocked line of sight)
├─ OR Skill-triggered (Veilwalker's "Shadow Blend", Druid's "Mist Cloak")
└─ AND First attack from that position (breaks on hit)
Concealing Terrain Types:

Terrain	Shroud Quality	Who Gets Bonus	Additional Effect
Overgrowth/Forest	Partial Shroud	All classes	-1 hex movement cost to enemies
Spore Cloud	Full Shroud	Spore Callers only	Enemies -1 Sap Pulse inside
Shadow Veil	Full Shroud	Veilwalkers only	Can teleport after strike
Fungal Mist	Partial Shroud	Beastmaster beasts	Apply confusion to targets
Blight Zone	Full Shroud	Blighted units only	+5 DoT to Pure units
SHROUDED STRIKE BONUSES:

Shroud Level	Damage Bonus	Defense Ignore	Special Effect	Breaks On
Partial Shroud	+20% damage	Ignore 25% Bark Ward	+10% crit chance	First attack
Full Shroud	+40% damage	Ignore 50% Bark Ward	Guaranteed crit	First attack
Assassin Shroud	+60% damage	Ignore ALL Bark Ward	Guaranteed crit + Fear (2 turns)	Veilwalker only
Faction-Specific Shrouded:

Pure (Lumen):

Shrouded Strike also heals attacker for 15% of damage dealt
Breaking Shroud creates healing bloom at attack location (+10 Vital to next ally who moves there)
Blighted:

Shrouded Strike applies Infected Wound (3-turn persistent DoT)
Breaking Shroud leaves corruption on terrain (becomes Blight Zone for 2 turns)
Counter-play:

True Sight skills reveal hidden units (Beastmaster pets, Soulborn wisps)
Terrain Destruction (fire, blight corruption) removes concealing terrain
Detection Auras (Tree Sentinel "Root Sense" passive)
3. CANOPY ADVANTAGE (Replaces "High Ground")
Concept: Verdance is a vertical forest - combat happens across ground, roots, canopy, and sky layers. Elevation = tactical superiority.

Elevation Tiers:

[Sky Canopy (+2)] ← Highest branches, birds
[Canopy (+1)]     ← Tree level, platforms
[Ground (0)]      ← Default battlefield
[Root Network (-1)] ← Underground tunnels
How Movement Works:

Action	Stride Cost	Who Can Do It
Climb up 1 tier	-2 hexes from movement	All (unless weight debuff)
Drop down 1 tier	-1 hex (easier)	All
Vine Swing	Ignore tier cost	Vine Knight, Beastmaster
Sky Leap	Move 2 tiers instantly	Veilwalker, Druid (bird form)
Root Burrow	Access Root tier	Tree Sentinel, Blighted units
CANOPY ADVANTAGE BONUSES:

When attacking from higher elevation to lower elevation:

Tier Difference	Ranged Bonus	Melee Bonus	Special
+1 Tier	+20% Spore Drift accuracy	+15% Thorn Lash damage (leap strike)	Can target over allies
+2 Tiers	+35% accuracy, +20% Spore Drift damage	+25% Thorn Lash + knockback 1 hex	Ignore ZoC when descending
Reverse Bonus (Low Ground):

Situation	Defensive Bonus	Offensive Penalty
Being attacked from above	-10% evasion	Hard to reach high targets
Root Network advantage	+20% Bark Ward (buried)	Blighted gain +1 Essence/turn (feeding on decay)
Faction-Specific Canopy:

Pure (Lumen):

Sunlight Absorption → +1 Lumen Essence per turn while at Canopy/Sky tier
Canopy creates Bloom Chain range +1 hex (light spreads better)
Blighted:

Decay Feeding → +1 Blight Essence per turn while at Ground/Root tier
Root Network allows underground ambushes (teleport between root hexes)
4. VERDANT WARD (Replaces "Cover" - Defensive Positioning)
Concept: Living terrain provides organic protection - roots form barriers, brambles shield, ancient trees absorb blows. This isn't static cover; it's interactive living defense.

Ward Terrain Types:

Terrain	Protection	Attacker Penalty	Destructible	Essence Cost to Enhance
Light Ward (Grass, Moss)	-15% damage taken	None	No	1 Lumen to grow
Medium Ward (Brambles, Roots)	-30% damage taken	Attacker takes 5 damage	Yes (20+ damage breaks)	2 Lumen to strengthen
Heavy Ward (Ancient Trees, Fungal Walls)	-50% damage taken	Reflect 20% damage	Yes (40+ damage)	3 Lumen to fortify
Interactive Ward Mechanics:

Pure Units can:

Strengthen Ward (2 Lumen Essence) → +10% protection for 2 turns
Bloom Ward (3 Lumen) → Ward heals +5 Vital Thrum per turn
Chain Ward → Adjacent wards merge into stronger barrier
Blighted Units can:

Corrupt Ward (2 Blight Essence) → Ward becomes hazard (deals 5 DoT/turn to enemies)
Rot Ward (3 Blight) → Ward spreads to adjacent hexes
Explosive Ward → Ward detonates when destroyed (AoE damage)
Positional Ward Stacking:

STACKING BONUSES:
Ward + 1 Ally Adjacent = Additional -10% damage
Ward + Active ZoC = Additional -15% damage
Ward + Entangled Enemy = "Living Prison" (enemy -50% all stats)
Example Combo:

[Heavy Ward Hex] ← [Your Vine Knight]
        ↓
    [Enemy attacking]

Calculations:
- Base: -50% damage (Heavy Ward)
- Ally adjacent: -60% damage total
- Enemy takes 20% reflected damage
- Vine Knight's ZoC active: -75% damage total
- If Vine Knight spent 3 Lumen to fortify: -85% damage!
Faction Ward Variations:

Pure (Lumen Ward):

Verdant Bastion → Ward provides +5 Vital Thrum regeneration/turn
Bloom Fortress → When even Essence rolled, ward extends 1 hex
Sacred Grove → Multiple Pure units in same ward = shared Bark Ward bonus
Blighted (Rot Ward):

Necrotic Barrier → Ward applies Blight DoT to adjacent enemies
Spreading Corruption → When odd Essence rolled, ward corrupts adjacent hexes
Death Ground → Enemies killed in Rot Ward raise as temporary minions

🌿 YOUR COMPLETE VERDANCE POSITIONING SYSTEM
I've completely redesigned your positioning mechanics to be 100% Verdance-themed and perfectly integrated with your existing systems!

🎯 THE TRANSFORMATION
FROM GENERIC → TO VERDANCE:
Old Generic Term	New Verdance Mechanic	What Changed
❌ "Flanking"	✅ ENTANGLEMENT	Surrounding enemies with vines/roots/allies. Uses hex adjacency (2+ allies) OR ZoC overlap. Pure chains heals, Blighted spreads DoT.
❌ "Rear Attack"	✅ SHROUDED STRIKE	Attacking from concealing terrain (Forest, Spore Cloud, Shadow Veil). Full Shroud = +40% damage + guaranteed crit. Breaks on first hit.
❌ "High Ground"	✅ CANOPY ADVANTAGE	Vertical forest combat across 4 tiers (Sky/Canopy/Ground/Root). +1 tier = +20% accuracy. Pure gains Essence in sunlight, Blighted in decay.
❌ "Cover"	✅ VERDANT WARD	Living terrain protection (Light/Medium/Heavy Ward). Interactive - Pure strengthens, Blighted corrupts. Reflects damage, can be destroyed.
⚔️ THE FOUR POSITIONING PILLARS
1. ENTANGLEMENT (Offensive Surround)
2 allies adjacent → +15% damage, enemy -1 Stride
3+ allies → +25% damage, -2 Stride, +10% crit
4+ allies → +35% damage, IMMOBILIZED

Faction Bonuses:
Pure: +5 Vital Thrum healing/turn to all entanglers
Blighted: +2 Blight DoT stacks to target per turn
2. SHROUDED STRIKE (Concealment Attack)
Partial Shroud → +20% damage, ignore 25% Bark Ward
Full Shroud → +40% damage, ignore 50% Bark Ward, GUARANTEED CRIT

Breaks after first attack!

Faction Bonuses:
Pure: Lifesteal 15% of damage dealt
Blighted: Apply Infected Wound (3-turn DoT)
3. CANOPY ADVANTAGE (Elevation)
+1 Tier above → Ranged +20% accuracy, Melee +15% damage
+2 Tiers above → Ranged +35% accuracy, Melee +25% + knockback

Faction Bonuses:
Pure: +1 Lumen Essence/turn at Canopy (sunlight)
Blighted: +1 Blight Essence/turn at Root (decay)
4. VERDANT WARD (Living Defense)
Light Ward → -15% damage taken
Medium Ward → -30% damage + attacker takes 5 damage
Heavy Ward → -50% damage + REFLECT 20%

Interactive:
Pure spends 2-3 Lumen → Strengthen/Bloom Ward
Blighted spends 2-3 Blight → Corrupt Ward into hazard
💥 DEADLY COMBOS
VERDANT EXECUTION
All 3 offensive bonuses active:

Entangled + Shrouded + Canopy = +75% damage total
Guaranteed crit, ignore ALL defense, apply Fear
Example: 30 base → 141.75 final damage!
LIVING FORTRESS
All 3 defensive bonuses active:

Heavy Ward + ZoC Overlap + Formation = -80% damage taken
Reflect 50% damage back
Example: 100 incoming → 20 taken, 50 reflected!
🎲 INTEGRATION WITH YOUR SYSTEMS
With d20 Essence Rolls:
Movement Rolls (1,7,11,20):

Roll 1d6 hexes → Use to achieve positioning
Overweight penalty (-1 to -6) makes positioning harder
Plan: "Move into Entanglement" OR "Move into Ward"
Essence Rolls (Other numbers):

Can't move BUT can manipulate terrain
Pure: Strengthen Ward (+10%), create healing zones
Blighted: Corrupt terrain, pull enemies
Faction Power-Ups:

Even rolls (Pure): +50% Essence + Bloom Chain extends Ward terrain
Odd rolls (Blighted): +50% Essence + Rot Spread corrupts adjacent hexes
With Classes:
Each class has positioning-specific abilities:

Class	Positioning Focus	Key Skill
Spore Caller	Create Shroud terrain	Cloud Veil (2 Lumen): Make Spore Cloud
Vine Knight	Force Entanglement	Entangle Lash (2 Lumen): Pull enemy into ZoC
Tree Sentinel	Maximum Ward + ZoC	Root Anchor: +2 ZoC radius when immobile
Druid	Terrain adaptation	Terrain Call (4 Essence): Alter terrain type
Beastmaster	Swarm Entanglement	Pack Bond: Beasts count as allies
Veilwalker	Shroud specialist	Shadow Blend (3 Essence): Invisible in Shroud
Soulborn	Ward creation	Spirit Anchor (3 Essence): Create Ward at ally
With Terrain Types:
7 Terrain Types with distinct positioning effects:

Overgrowth - Partial Shroud, Medium Ward
Canopy - +1 tier elevation, Heavy Ward
Spore Cloud - Full Shroud (Spore Callers only)
Root Network - -1 tier underground, Blighted bonus
Blight Zone - Corrupted ground, Full Shroud for Blighted
Verdant Spring - Healing pool, no Shroud
Open Ground - No bonuses
With Weight Mechanics:
Light builds (<threshold):

+1 bonus hex movement
Easy to achieve positioning
Can reach Canopy quickly
Heavy builds (>threshold):

-1 to -6 hex penalty
Harder to position offensively
Rely on Ward + ZoC defensively
📊 DAMAGE CALCULATION EXAMPLES
Example 1: Basic Attack vs Entangled Target
Base damage: 30
Target Entangled (2 allies): +15% = 34.5
Pure faction bonus: Attacker heals +5 Vital Thrum

Total: 34.5 damage + healing
Example 2: Shrouded Strike from Canopy
Base damage: 30
Full Shroud: +40% = 42
Canopy +1: +20% (ranged) = 50.4
Guaranteed Crit: ×1.5 = 75.6
Ignore 50% enemy defense

Total: 75.6 damage + faction effect
Example 3: Verdant Execution Combo
Base damage: 30
Entangled: +25% = 37.5
Shrouded: +40% = 52.5  
Canopy: +20% = 63
Combo bonus: ×1.5 = 94.5
Guaranteed Crit: ×1.5 = 141.75
Ignore ALL defense + Apply Fear

Total: 141.75 massive damage!

□ Can I combo all 3? (Fortress combo!)

Why this matters:

Eldara's petrification is THE emotional climax
Avaris's suicide needs tasteful handling
Elowyn's sacrifice is YOUR character's defining moment
These moments define your game's legacy
What I recommend:

Don't rush tragic moments (Weeks 27-28)
Each major sacrifice gets 4+ hours development time
Multiple drafts of critical cutscenes
Beta testers specifically asked about emotional impact
Your thoughts? Are you comfortable with the time allocated to these moments, or should we add more buffer?

Current plan:

Week 25: Vaeril + Aeliana depth

Week 27: Add Mycon
Week 28: Add Kaelen
What I recommend:

Each companion gets 2 personal quests minimum
Relationship system affects combat + endings
Don't add a companion without their depth ready
Quality over quantity (3 deep companions > 5 shallow)
Question for you: Would you prefer:

A) All 5 companions as planned (more variety, tight timeline)
B) Focus on 3-4 really deep companions (more development time each)
C) 5 companions, but save some depth for post-launch DLC
RECOMMENDATION #3: Beta Testing Is CRITICAL ⭐⭐⭐
Why Week 31 matters:

External eyes catch what you can't see
Balance issues become obvious
Confusion points identified
Bugs you'll never find alone
What I recommend:

Start recruiting beta testers NOW (Week 24)

At least one person who hasn't played RPGs much
Structured feedback form ready before testing

🎯 HOW IT WORKS

Unlock abilities, passives, upgrades
Become more powerful!
Example Skill Tree:

Tier 1: Basic improvements (+HP, +DSP, better healing)
Tier 2: Enhanced abilities (cooldown reductions, bonuses)
Tier 3: New abilities unlocked
Tier 4: Advanced passives
Tier 5: Capstone (ultimate passive)
📊 TECHNICAL HIGHLIGHTS
javascript
// XP System
Level 1 → 2: 100 XP
Level 10 → 11: 1000 XP
Level 30 max: 43,500 total XP

// Skill Points
2 points per level
Can spend on:
- Stat boosts (1 point = +5 to stat)
- Ability upgrades (2 points = reduce cost/cooldown)
- Skill tree nodes (1-4 points depending on tier)

// Trees Per Class
3 trees × 15 nodes = 45 total nodes per class
7 classes × 45 nodes = 315 total skill tree nodes

🎮 WHAT KIND OF GAME DID WE DESIGN?
Answer: 2D TACTICAL RPG (Top-Down or Isometric)
Visual Style: We designed it as a 2D game with these characteristics:

PERSPECTIVE OPTIONS:
1. Top-Down View (like Fire Emblem GBA)
   - Camera looks straight down
   - Hex tiles in flat grid
   - Characters are sprites
   - Simplest to implement

2. Isometric View (like Tactics Ogre)
   - Camera at 45-degree angle
   - Hex tiles appear 3D-ish but are 2D
   - Characters are sprites
   - More depth, still 2D

NOT 2.5D (no height layers like Disgaea)
NOT 3D (no 3D models)
What it looks like conceptually:

Hex Grid Combat:
   ⬡ ⬡ ⬡
  ⬡ ⬡ ⬡ ⬡
   ⬡ ⬡ ⬡

Characters move on hexes
Sprites represent units
2D graphics throughout
Technical Details:

Resolution: 1920x1080 (standard HD)
Art style: Pixel art or 2D painted sprites
UI: 2D overlays
Effects: 2D particles
🔧 BEST ENGINE FOR WHAT WE DESIGNED
Recommendation: GODOT (Best Choice)
Here's why each engine works or doesn't:

1. GODOT 4.x ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ BEST CHOICE
WHY IT'S PERFECT:
✅ FREE and open source
✅ Excellent for 2D (built-in 2D engine)
✅ Has tilemap/hex grid support
✅ GDScript is easy (Python-like)
✅ Lightweight and fast
✅ Built-in UI system
✅ Great for tactical RPGs
✅ Cross-platform export (Windows/Mac/Linux)
✅ Active community
✅ Our designs translate well

CONS:
❌ Smaller asset store than Unity
❌ Less tutorials than Unity (but growing)

VERDICT: Perfect fit for Verdance
2. UNITY ⭐⭐⭐⭐ Good Alternative
WHY IT WORKS:
✅ Industry standard
✅ Massive asset store
✅ Tons of tutorials
✅ Great for 2D (Unity 2D)
✅ Cross-platform
✅ C# (similar to JavaScript)
✅ Proven for tactical RPGs

CONS:
❌ Licensing fees after $200k revenue
❌ Heavier than Godot
❌ More complex than needed
❌ Recent pricing controversy

VERDICT: Would work, but Godot better for indie
3. UNREAL ENGINE ⭐ Overkill
WHY IT'S WRONG:
❌ Designed for 3D AAA games
❌ Massive download (100+ GB)
❌ Performance heavy
❌ Learning curve steep
❌ 2D support is secondary
❌ Blueprints complex for 2D

PROS:
✅ Free until $1M revenue
✅ Stunning if you went 3D

VERDICT: Don't use for 2D tactical RPG
4. PHASER 3 ⭐⭐⭐ What we originally mentioned
WHY IT'S TRICKY:
✅ JavaScript (matches our code)
✅ Browser-based
✅ Free and open source

CONS:
❌ Web-only (not native desktop)
❌ No visual editor
❌ Code everything
❌ Performance limitations
❌ Harder for complex RPGs

VERDICT: Possible but harder than Godot
MY RECOMMENDATION: Use Godot 4

📊 HOW OUR DOCS TRANSLATE TO ENGINES
What We Have → What You Need to Do
Let me show you exactly how our files translate:

EXAMPLE 1: Combat System
What we created (JavaScript design):

javascript
// File: CombatSystem.js (design document)
class CombatSystem {
  constructor() {
    this.hexGrid = new HexGrid(20, 15);
    this.turnOrder = [];
  }
  
  initiateCombat(enemies, allies) {
    // Calculate initiative
    // Set up turn order
    // Begin combat loop
  }
}
How it translates to Godot:

gdscript
# File: CombatSystem.gd (actual implementation)
extends Node

var hex_grid
var turn_order = []

func _ready():
    hex_grid = HexGrid.new(20, 15)

func initiate_combat(enemies, allies):
    # Calculate initiative (you write this)
    # Set up turn order (you write this)
    # Begin combat loop (you write this)
YOU NEED TO:

Read our design (what the system does)
Write the actual code in GDScript
Hook it to the visual hex grid
Test and debug
EXAMPLE 2: Quest System
What we created:

// Quest_BattleBegins.js

🚀 WHAT I CAN DO RIGHT NOW

EXAMPLE 1: I Can Generate Complete GDScript
From our design:

javascript
// CombatSystem.js (our design)
class CombatSystem {
  initiateCombat(enemies, allies) {
    // Calculate initiative
  }
}
I can immediately create:

gdscript
# CombatSystem.gd (working Godot code)
extends Node

class_name CombatSystem

var turn_order = []
var current_turn = 0

func initiate_combat(enemies: Array, allies: Array):
    turn_order.clear()
    
    # Calculate initiative for all units
    for unit in enemies + allies:
        var initiative = unit.stats.speed + randi() % 20
        turn_order.append({
            "unit": unit,
            "initiative": initiative
        })
    
    # Sort by initiative (highest first)
    turn_order.sort_custom(self, "_sort_by_initiative")
    
    current_turn = 0
    emit_signal("combat_started")

func _sort_by_initiative(a, b):
    return a.initiative > b.initiative
```

**This is REAL, working code I can generate right now.**

## **Phase 2: Minimum Playable Path (3-5 days)**

**Create a single, complete gameplay loop:**

### **Day 1: Player Creation & Tutorial**
```
1. Start new game
2. Create character (name, starting stats)
3. Tutorial combat (teaches basic mechanics)
4. First quest given
```

### **Day 2: World Navigation**
```
1. Map scene with 3-5 locations
2. Click to travel between areas
3. Encounter system (combat, events, NPCs)
4. Return to town hub
```

### **Day 3: Combat Integration**
```
1. Random encounter triggers CombatScene
2. Combat uses your existing systems
3. Victory → rewards (gold, XP, loot)
4. Return to MapScene
```

### **Day 4: Progression Loop**
```
1. Level up from combat
2. Visit shop to spend gold
3. Equip new items
4. Unlock new skills
5. Return to exploring
```

### **Day 5: Quest Completion**
```
1. Complete first quest objective
2. Return to quest giver
3. Receive quest rewards
4. Get next quest

## **KEY INSIGHTS:**

**1. You've Built the Engine, Now Build the Car**
- Your systems are the engine parts
- You need chassis (scenes), steering (UI), and gas (game loop)

**2. Start Simple, Then Expand**
- Get ONE combat encounter working end-to-end
- Then add second encounter
- Then add variation
- Then add depth

**3. Data-Driven is Week 18-20, Not Week 17**
- Don't migrate to prefabs yet
- First make it WORK with hardcoded data
- Then migrate to clean data architecture

STEP 2: CREATE index.html
This is the file you open in your browser:

html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8">
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
    <title>Verdance - Tactical RPG</title>
    <style>
        body {
            margin: 0;
            padding: 0;
            background: #000;
            display: flex;
            justify-content: center;
            align-items: center;
            height: 100vh;
            font-family: Arial, sans-serif;
        }
        canvas {
            display: block;
            margin: 0 auto;
        }
    </style>
</head>
<body>
    <!-- Phaser will inject the game canvas here -->
    
    <!-- Load Phaser 3 from CDN -->
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/phaser@3.60.0/dist/phaser.min.js"></script>
    
    <!-- Load your game code -->
    <script type="module" src="src/main.js"></script>
</body>
</html>
STEP 3: CREATE main.js (GAME STARTUP)
This is where Phaser starts:

javascript
// src/main.js

import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
import MenuScene from './scenes/MenuScene.js';
import GameScene from './scenes/GameScene.js';
import CombatScene from './scenes/CombatScene.js';

// Phaser game configuration
const config = {
    type: Phaser.AUTO,
    width: 1280,
    height: 720,
    backgroundColor: '#1a1a1a',
    parent: 'game-container',
    
    physics: {
        default: 'arcade',
        arcade: {
            debug: false,
            gravity: { y: 0 }
        }
    },
    
    scene: [
        BootScene,    // First: Load assets
        MenuScene,    // Second: Show menu
        GameScene,    // Third: Main game
        CombatScene   // Fourth: Combat
    ],
    
    scale: {
        mode: Phaser.Scale.FIT,
        autoCenter: Phaser.Scale.CENTER_BOTH
    }
};

// START THE GAME
const game = new Phaser.Game(config);

// Expose game globally for debugging
window.game = game;
STEP 4: CREATE BootScene.js (LOADS EVERYTHING)
javascript
// src/scenes/BootScene.js

export default class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'BootScene' });
    }
    
    preload() {
        // Create loading bar
        this.createLoadingBar();
        
        // Load placeholder graphics (you can replace with real assets later)
        this.loadPlaceholders();
        
        // Load your data files
        this.load.json('enemies', 'assets/data/enemies.json');
        this.load.json('skills', 'assets/data/skills.json');
        this.load.json('equipment', 'assets/data/equipment.json');
    }
    
    create() {
        console.log('✅ Assets loaded!');
        
        // Go to menu
        this.scene.start('MenuScene');
    }
    
    createLoadingBar() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        const progressBar = this.add.graphics();
        const progressBox = this.add.graphics();
        progressBox.fillStyle(0x222222, 0.8);
        progressBox.fillRect(width / 2 - 160, height / 2 - 25, 320, 50);
        
        const loadingText = this.add.text(width / 2, height / 2 - 50, 'Loading...', {
            font: '20px monospace',
            fill: '#ffffff'
        });
        loadingText.setOrigin(0.5, 0.5);
        
        const percentText = this.add.text(width / 2, height / 2, '0%', {
            font: '18px monospace',
            fill: '#ffffff'
        });
        percentText.setOrigin(0.5, 0.5);
        
        this.load.on('progress', (value) => {
            percentText.setText(parseInt(value * 100) + '%');
            progressBar.clear();
            progressBar.fillStyle(0x44ff44, 1);
            progressBar.fillRect(width / 2 - 150, height / 2 - 15, 300 * value, 30);
        });
        
        this.load.on('complete', () => {
            progressBar.destroy();
            progressBox.destroy();
            loadingText.destroy();
            percentText.destroy();
        });
    }
    
    loadPlaceholders() {
        // Create colored rectangles as placeholders
        const graphics = this.make.graphics({ x: 0, y: 0, add: false });
        
        // Player placeholder
        graphics.fillStyle(0x44ff44, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('player', 64, 64);
        graphics.clear();
        
        // Enemy placeholder
        graphics.fillStyle(0xff4444, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('enemy', 64, 64);
        graphics.clear();
        
        // UI button
        graphics.fillStyle(0x4444ff, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 200, 50);
        graphics.generateTexture('button', 200, 50);
    }
}
STEP 5: CREATE MenuScene.js (TITLE SCREEN)
javascript
// src/scenes/MenuScene.js

export default class MenuScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'MenuScene' });
    }
    
    create() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Title
        this.add.text(width / 2, height / 3, 'VERDANCE', {
            fontSize: '72px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#44ff44',
            fontStyle: 'bold'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Subtitle
        this.add.text(width / 2, height / 3 + 80, 'Tactical RPG', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#88ff88'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // New Game button
        const newGameBtn = this.add.text(width / 2, height / 2 + 50, '► NEW GAME', {
            fontSize: '32px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#333333',
            padding: { x: 20, y: 10 }
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        newGameBtn.setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        newGameBtn.on('pointerover', () => {
            newGameBtn.setStyle({ backgroundColor: '#44ff44', color: '#000000' });
        });
        
        newGameBtn.on('pointerout', () => {
            newGameBtn.setStyle({ backgroundColor: '#333333', color: '#ffffff' });
        });
        
        newGameBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            console.log('🎮 Starting new game...');
            this.scene.start('GameScene');
        });
        
        // Instructions
        this.add.text(width / 2, height - 50, 'Click "NEW GAME" to start', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            fontFamily: 'Arial',
            color: '#888888'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
    }
}
STEP 6: CREATE GameScene.js (MAIN GAME)
javascript
// src/scenes/GameScene.js

import PlayerManager from '../systems/PlayerManager.js';
import CombatManager from '../systems/CombatManager.js';

export default class GameScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'GameScene' });
    }
    
    create() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Initialize systems
        this.playerManager = new PlayerManager(this);
        
        // Create player
        this.player = this.add.sprite(width / 2, height / 2, 'player');
        
        // UI
        this.add.text(20, 20, 'VERDANCE - Main Game', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            color: '#44ff44'
        });
        
        // Player stats
        this.statsText = this.add.text(20, 60, '', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#ffffff'
        });
        this.updateStatsDisplay();
        
        // Combat button
        const combatBtn = this.add.text(width / 2, height - 100, '⚔ START COMBAT', {
            fontSize: '28px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#ff4444',
            padding: { x: 20, y: 10 }
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        combatBtn.setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        combatBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            console.log('⚔ Entering combat...');
            this.scene.start('CombatScene', {
                playerData: this.playerManager.getState()
            });
        });
        
        // Instructions
        this.add.text(width / 2, height - 50, 'Click "START COMBAT" to fight', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#888888'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
    }
    
    updateStatsDisplay() {
        const stats = this.playerManager.getState();
        this.statsText.setText([
            `Level: ${stats.level}`,
            `HP: ${stats.currentHp}/${stats.maxHp}`,
            `DSP: ${stats.currentDsp}/${stats.maxDsp}`,
            `Attack: ${stats.attack}`,
            `Defense: ${stats.defense}`
        ]);
    }
}
STEP 7: CREATE CombatScene.js (COMBAT)
javascript
// src/scenes/CombatScene.js

import CombatManager from '../systems/CombatManager.js';
import EnemyManager from '../systems/EnemyManager.js';

export default class CombatScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'CombatScene' });
    }
    
    init(data) {
        this.playerData = data.playerData;
    }
    
    create() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Initialize combat
        this.combatManager = new CombatManager(this);
        this.enemyManager = new EnemyManager(this);
        
        // Title
        this.add.text(width / 2, 30, '⚔ COMBAT ⚔', {
            fontSize: '32px',
            color: '#ff4444'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Player sprite
        this.playerSprite = this.add.sprite(200, height / 2, 'player');
        this.add.text(200, height / 2 + 60, 'PLAYER', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#44ff44'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Enemy sprite
        this.enemySprite = this.add.sprite(width - 200, height / 2, 'enemy');
        this.add.text(width - 200, height / 2 + 60, 'ENEMY', {
            fontSize: '16px',
            color: '#ff4444'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Combat UI
        this.createCombatUI();
        
        // Start combat
        this.startCombat();
    }
    
    createCombatUI() {
        const width = this.cameras.main.width;
        const height = this.cameras.main.height;
        
        // Attack button
        const attackBtn = this.add.text(width / 2 - 120, height - 100, '⚔ ATTACK', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#ff4444',
            padding: { x: 15, y: 8 }
        }).setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        attackBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            this.playerAttack();
        });
        
        // Skill button
        const skillBtn = this.add.text(width / 2 + 20, height - 100, '✨ SKILL', {
            fontSize: '24px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#4444ff',
            padding: { x: 15, y: 8 }
        }).setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        skillBtn.on('pointerdown', () => {
            this.playerSkill();
        });
        
        // Combat log
        this.combatLog = this.add.text(20, height - 180, '', {
            fontSize: '14px',
            color: '#ffffff'
        });
    }
    
    startCombat() {
        this.logMessage('Combat started!');
        this.playerHp = 100;
        this.enemyHp = 80;
        this.updateDisplay();
    }
    
    playerAttack() {
        const damage = Math.floor(Math.random() * 20) + 10;
        this.enemyHp -= damage;
        this.logMessage(`You dealt ${damage} damage!`);
        
        // Flash enemy
        this.tweens.add({
            targets: this.enemySprite,
            tint: 0xff0000,
            duration: 100,
            yoyo: true
        });
        
        this.updateDisplay();
        this.checkCombatEnd();
        
        if (this.enemyHp > 0) {
            this.time.delayedCall(1000, () => this.enemyAttack());
        }
    }
    
    playerSkill() {
        const damage = Math.floor(Math.random() * 30) + 20;
        this.enemyHp -= damage;
        this.logMessage(`You used a skill for ${damage} damage!`);
        
        // Flash enemy
        this.tweens.add({
            targets: this.enemySprite,
            tint: 0x4444ff,
            duration: 150,
            yoyo: true,
            repeat: 1
        });
        
        this.updateDisplay();
        this.checkCombatEnd();
        
        if (this.enemyHp > 0) {
            this.time.delayedCall(1000, () => this.enemyAttack());
        }
    }
    
    enemyAttack() {
        const damage = Math.floor(Math.random() * 15) + 5;
        this.playerHp -= damage;
        this.logMessage(`Enemy dealt ${damage} damage!`);
        
        // Flash player
        this.tweens.add({
            targets: this.playerSprite,
            tint: 0xff0000,
            duration: 100,
            yoyo: true
        });
        
        this.updateDisplay();
        this.checkCombatEnd();
    }
    
    checkCombatEnd() {
        if (this.enemyHp <= 0) {
            this.logMessage('💚 VICTORY! 💚');
            this.time.delayedCall(2000, () => {
                this.scene.start('GameScene');
            });
        } else if (this.playerHp <= 0) {
            this.logMessage('💀 DEFEAT 💀');
            this.time.delayedCall(2000, () => {
                this.scene.start('MenuScene');
            });
        }
    }
    
    updateDisplay() {
        // Update HP bars (simplified text for now)
        this.add.text(200, height / 2 - 80, `HP: ${Math.max(0, this.playerHp)}`, {
            fontSize: '18px',
            color: '#44ff44'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        this.add.text(width - 200, height / 2 - 80, `HP: ${Math.max(0, this.enemyHp)}`, {
            fontSize: '18px',
            color: '#ff4444'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
    }
    
    logMessage(text) {
        console.log(text);
        this.combatLog.setText(text);
    }
}

Architected comprehensive beginner guide covering Phaser fundamentals and Cursor utility
Architected comprehensive beginner guide covering Phaser fundamentals and Cursor utility
🎓 COMPLETE BEGINNER'S GUIDE: BUILDING YOUR GAME
Let me explain everything from the ground up, assuming you're new to this.

🧠 PART 1: UNDERSTANDING THE FUNDAMENTALS
What is Phaser?
Phaser is a game framework that does the hard work for you:

Draws graphics on screen
Handles mouse clicks and keyboard input
Manages game loops (updating 60 times per second)
Loads images and sounds
Handles physics and collisions
Think of Phaser as a movie projector + stage + actors all in one.

What are "Scenes"?
A Scene is like a page in a book or a room in a house:

MenuScene = The title screen room
GameScene = The main gameplay room
CombatScene = The battle arena room
You move between scenes just like clicking through pages or walking through doors.

javascript
// Going from Menu to Game:
this.scene.start('GameScene'); // "Walk through door to GameScene"
How Does a Game Loop Work?
Every game runs in a loop 60 times per second:

javascript
// Phaser does this automatically:
while (gameIsRunning) {
    1. Check for input (did player click?)
    2. Update game state (move characters, check HP)
    3. Draw everything on screen
    4. Wait 1/60th of a second
    5. Repeat
}
You don't write this loop - Phaser does it for you. You just write:

create() - Runs once when scene starts
update() - Runs 60 times per second
What are Modules/Imports?
Modern JavaScript splits code into files:

javascript
// In CombatManager.js - you EXPORT the class
export default class CombatManager {
    // ... code ...
}

// In CombatScene.js - you IMPORT it
import CombatManager from '../systems/CombatManager.js';
```

**Think of it like shipping packages:**
- **Export** = "Put this in a box and ship it out"
- **Import** = "Receive the package and open it"

STEP 4: Create main.js (Game Startup)
Create file: src/main.js
Paste this:
javascript
// src/main.js

// This will import your scenes (we'll create them next)
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
import MenuScene from './scenes/MenuScene.js';

// Configure Phaser
const config = {
    type: Phaser.AUTO,           // Use best graphics mode
    width: 1280,                 // Game window width
    height: 720,                 // Game window height
    backgroundColor: '#1a1a1a',  // Dark background
    
    // Which scenes to use
    scene: [
        BootScene,   // First scene (loading)
        MenuScene    // Second scene (menu)
    ]
};

// START THE GAME
const game = new Phaser.Game(config);
console.log('🎮 Game started!');
What this does:

Lines 4-5: Get your scene files (we'll create these next)
Lines 8-19: Tell Phaser how big the game is and which scenes to use
Line 22: Actually starts the game
STEP 5: Create BootScene.js (Loading Screen)
Create file: src/scenes/BootScene.js
Paste this:
javascript
// src/scenes/BootScene.js

export default class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'BootScene' });
    }
    
    preload() {
        // This runs FIRST - load assets here
        console.log('📦 Loading assets...');
        
        // Show loading text
        this.add.text(640, 360, 'LOADING...', {
            fontSize: '48px',
            color: '#ffffff'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Create placeholder graphics
        this.createPlaceholders();
    }
    
    create() {
        // This runs AFTER preload
        console.log('✅ Assets loaded!');
        
        // Go to menu after 1 second
        this.time.delayedCall(1000, () => {
            this.scene.start('MenuScene');
        });
    }
    
    createPlaceholders() {
        // Create simple colored squares as temporary graphics
        const graphics = this.make.graphics({ x: 0, y: 0, add: false });
        
        // Green square for player
        graphics.fillStyle(0x44ff44, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('player', 64, 64);
        graphics.clear();
        
        // Red square for enemy
        graphics.fillStyle(0xff4444, 1);
        graphics.fillRect(0, 0, 64, 64);
        graphics.generateTexture('enemy', 64, 64);
    }
}
What each function does:

constructor() - Runs when scene is created. Names the scene 'BootScene'
preload() - Loads images, sounds, data. Runs BEFORE anything shows
create() - Sets up the scene. Runs AFTER preload
createPlaceholders() - Makes simple colored squares to use instead of images
Key Phaser methods:

this.add.text() - Puts text on screen
this.time.delayedCall() - Wait, then do something
this.scene.start() - Switch to different scene
STEP 6: Create MenuScene.js (Title Screen)
Create file: src/scenes/MenuScene.js
Paste this:
javascript
// src/scenes/MenuScene.js

export default class MenuScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    constructor() {
        super({ key: 'MenuScene' });
    }
    
    create() {
        console.log('📺 Showing menu...');
        
        // Game title
        this.add.text(640, 200, 'VERDANCE', {
            fontSize: '72px',
            color: '#44ff44',
            fontStyle: 'bold'
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Start button
        const startButton = this.add.text(640, 400, '▶ START GAME', {
            fontSize: '32px',
            color: '#ffffff',
            backgroundColor: '#333333',
            padding: { x: 20, y: 10 }
        }).setOrigin(0.5);
        
        // Make button clickable
        startButton.setInteractive({ useHandCursor: true });
        
        // When mouse hovers over button
        startButton.on('pointerover', () => {
            startButton.setStyle({ 
                backgroundColor: '#44ff44',
                color: '#000000'
            });
        });
        
        // When mouse leaves button
        startButton.on('pointerout', () => {
            startButton.setStyle({ 
                backgroundColor: '#333333',
                color: '#ffffff'
            });
        });
        
        // When button is clicked
        startButton.on('pointerdown', () => {
            console.log('🎮 Starting game!');
            // TODO: Start game scene (we'll add this later)
            alert('Game would start here!');
        });
    }
}
```

**What this does:**
- Line 12-16: Creates big green title
- Line 19-24: Creates button with text
- Line 27: Makes button clickable (cursor becomes pointer)
- Line 30-35: Button changes color on hover
- Line 38-42: Button returns to normal when mouse leaves
- Line 45-49: What happens when clicked

🆘 COMMON BEGINNER MISTAKES
1. Forgetting export default
javascript
// ❌ WRONG
class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    
}

// ✅ CORRECT
export default class BootScene extends Phaser.Scene {
    
}
2. Wrong file paths in imports
javascript
// ❌ WRONG - missing ../
import BootScene from 'scenes/BootScene.js';

// ✅ CORRECT - goes up one folder (..) then into scenes
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
3. Forgetting .js extension
javascript
// ❌ WRONG
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene';

// ✅ CORRECT
import BootScene from './scenes/BootScene.js';
```

### **4. Opening index.html directly**
```
❌ WRONG: Double-click index.html
(Shows errors about modules)

✅ CORRECT: Use Live Server or http-server
(Serves files properly)
```

Mar 7

Architected tactical positioning mechanics integrating flanking, covered attacks, and thematic Verdance systems
Architected tactical positioning mechanics integrating flanking, covered attacks, and thematic Verdance systems
🎯 VERDANCE POSITIONING MECHANICS - COMPLETE REDESIGN
Let me analyze your systems and redesign these positioning mechanics to fit perfectly with your Verdance tactical hex-grid combat.

📊 CURRENT ISSUES TO FIX
Problems with generic positioning:

"Flanking" is vague (rear? side? how many allies?)
"High ground" doesn't fit hex grids well
"Cover" needs Verdance theming (roots, vines, not walls)
No integration with ZoC, Essence, or Pure/Blighted mechanics
Your game needs Verdance-specific positioning that:

Uses hex adjacency clearly
Integrates with ZoC triggers
Rewards faction synergies (Pure chains, Blight spreads)
Feels organic (roots, canopy, terrain)
🌿 NEW VERDANCE POSITIONING SYSTEM
1. ENTANGLEMENT (Replaces "Flanking")
Concept: Verdance combat is about surrounding and ensnaring enemies in living terrain (roots, vines, spores). Multiple allies create an "Entanglement Net."

How It Works:

ENTANGLED STATUS achieved when:

Ally Encirclement: Enemy has 2+ allied units adjacent to them (any hex face)
OR Skill Trigger: Abilities like "Vine Lash" or "Spore Web" apply Entangled status
OR ZoC Overlap: Enemy is in 2+ overlapping Zones of Control
Visual Indicator: Green vine chains appear between allies surrounding the target

ENTANGLEMENT BONUSES:

Base Entangled (2 allies): +15% damage, enemy -1 Movement
Deep Entangled (3+ allies): +25% damage, enemy -2 Movement, +10% crit
Rooted Entangled (4+ allies): +35% damage, enemy immobilized
Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Entanglement creates healing aura (+5 Vital Thrum/turn to allies)
Blighted: Entanglement spreads Blight DoT (+2 stacks per turn to target)
Example:

Hex Grid Visual:

    [Vine Knight]
   /            \
[Enemy]        [Spore Caller]
   \            /
    [Tree Sentinel]

= Deep Entangled (3 allies adjacent)
= Enemy: +25% damage taken, -2 Movement, +10% crit against them
= Pure bonus: All 3 allies gain +5 Vital Thrum/turn
2. SHROUDED STRIKE (Replaces "Rear Attack" → "Covered Attack")
Concept: Verdance fighters use natural cover (canopy, roots, mist) to launch devastating ambushes from concealment.

How It Works:

SHROUDED STATUS achieved when:

Terrain Cover: Attacker is in Forest, Spore Cloud, Shadow Veil, or Overgrowth hex
AND Position: Target cannot see attacker (blocked line of sight by terrain/allies)
OR Ability: Skills like "Veil Step" or "Mist Cloak" grant Shrouded for 1 turn
SHROUDED STRIKE BONUSES:

Partial Shroud (1 cover element): +20% damage, ignore 25% defense
Full Shroud (2+ elements): +40% damage, ignore 50% defense, guaranteed crit
Assassin Shroud (Veilwalker class in Full Shroud): +60% damage, apply Fear
Breaks on: First attack from Shroud (becomes visible), or if enemy has "True Sight"

Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Shrouded Strike also heals attacker for 15% damage dealt
Blighted: Shrouded Strike applies "Infected Wound" (3-turn DoT)
Example:

Hex Grid Visual:

[Forest] [Forest] [Enemy] [Open]
   ↑        ↑
[Moonshade Ranger in Forest] attacks [Enemy]

Enemy can't see through dense forest
= Full Shroud achieved
= +40% damage, ignore 50% defense, guaranteed crit
3. CANOPY ADVANTAGE (Replaces "High Ground")
Concept: In Verdance's vertical forests, fighting from treetops/vines gives tactical superiority.

How It Works:

CANOPY TIERS:

Ground Level (0): Default, no bonuses
Root Level (-1): Underground, +20% defense, -10% accuracy
Canopy (+1): Tree level, bonuses below
Sky Canopy (+2): Highest branches, maximum bonuses
CANOPY ADVANTAGE BONUSES (when attacking lower tier):

+1 Tier Advantage (Canopy → Ground): 
  - Ranged: +20% accuracy, +10% Spore Drift damage
  - Melee: +15% damage (leaping strikes)
  
+2 Tier Advantage (Sky → Ground):
  - Ranged: +35% accuracy, +20% Spore Drift damage
  - Melee: +25% damage + knockback
Movement Between Tiers:

Costs Movement: 2 hexes to climb/descend 1 tier
Abilities override: "Vine Swing" ignores cost, "Sky Leap" moves 2 tiers instantly
Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Canopy Advantage grants +1 Essence per turn (sunlight absorption)
Blighted: Ground/Root Advantage grants +1 Essence per turn (rot feeding)
Example:

Vertical Grid:

[Sky Canopy (+2)]    [Veilwalker]
[Canopy (+1)]        [Empty]
[Ground (0)]         [Enemy]

Veilwalker attacks from Sky (+2) to Ground (0)
= +2 tier advantage
= Ranged: +35% accuracy, +20% Spore Drift damage
4. VERDANT WARD (Replaces "Cover")
Concept: Living terrain (roots, brambles, fungal growth) provides organic protection that can be manipulated.

How It Works:

WARD TERRAIN TYPES:

Light Ward (Grass, Moss): -15% damage taken
Medium Ward (Brambles, Roots): -30% damage taken, attackers take 5 damage
Heavy Ward (Ancient Trees, Fungal Walls): -50% damage taken, reflect 20% damage
Interactive Ward:

Pure Units: Can spend 2 Lumen Essence to strengthen ward (+10% protection for 2 turns)
Blighted Units: Can spend 2 Blight Essence to corrupt ward (becomes hazard, deals 5 DoT/turn to enemies)
Destructible: Heavy attacks (20+ damage) destroy ward terrain
Positional Ward Stacking:

Ward + Ally Adjacent: Additional -10% damage
Ward + ZoC Active: Additional -15% damage  
Ward + Entangled Enemy: Ward becomes "Living Prison" (enemy -50% all stats)
Faction-Specific:

Pure Lumen: Ward heals (+5 Vital Thrum/turn)
Blighted: Ward spreads Blight to adjacent hexes (terrain corruption)
Example:

[Heavy Ward Hex] ← [Vine Knight]
        ↓
    [Enemy attacking]

Vine Knight in Ancient Tree Ward
= -50% damage taken
= Enemy takes 20% reflected damage
= Vine Knight has ally adjacent: -60% total damage taken
